```
2: 
3: ## 1. Project Overview & Objectives
4: The goal is to build a high-fidelity, functional clone of the Harbour.Space application ecosystem. This includes the public-facing marketing layer, the application/lead funnel, the authenticated student portal reflecting the unique 3-week modular learning schedule, and background operational workflows (Mock CRM & Email).

6: ---
7: 
8: ## 2. Epics & Functional Requirements
9: 
10: ### Epic 1: Marketing & Program Pages (Logged-Out)
11: *   **Homepage:** Premium landing experience capturing the "Tech, Entrepreneurship, and Design" brand ethos. Features global campus indicators (Barcelona & Bangkok) and key statistics (e.g., ICPC Gold Medallists, 95% Employability).
12: *   **Program Catalog & Detail Pages:** Dynamic routing for degrees across Technology (Computer Science, Data Science, Front-End) and Creative tracks (Interaction Design, High-Tech Entrepreneurship).
13:     *   *Requirement:* Display the "14 modules, 3 weeks per module" learning structure visually.
14: *   **Call-to-Action (CTA) & Lead Capture:** Interactive "Apply Now" and "Download Brochure" modals/flows capturing user contact information.
15: 
16: ### Epic 2: Authentication & Multi-Role Experience
17: *   **Authentication Flow:** JWT or session-based Login/Signup experience. 
18: *   **Logged-In Dashboard (Student Hub):**
19:     *   **Current Module View:** Displays the active 3-week course, remaining days, assigned industry mentor, and daily schedule (3 hours of interactive sessions/day).
20:     *   **Academic Timeline:** Progress track across the 14 yearly modules (Completed, Active, Upcoming).
21:     *   **Profile/Documents:** Status of English proficiency certificate, transcripts, and visa handling checklist.
22: 
23: ### Epic 3: Mock CRM & Admin Management
24: *   **Admin Dashboard:** A simple interface to view leads generated by the marketing CTA flows.
25: *   **Application Pipeline:** Track applications moving through stages: `Submitted` ➔ `Interview Scheduled` ➔ `Accepted` ➔ `Enrolled`.
26: *   **Data Persistence:** Store lead profiles (Name, Email, Program Interest, Campus Choice) in a unified database schema.
27: 
28: ### Epic 4: Analytics, Automation & Mock Workflows
29: *   **Mock Email Service:** An internal portal/logger showing outbound automated emails triggered by user actions:
30:     *   *Trigger A:* "Application Received" instant confirmation email upon submitting an application.
31:     *   *Trigger B:* "Interview Invitation" from the admissions team once an admin advances their status.
32: *   **Analytics Dashboard:** Frontend event logging tracking clicks on "Apply Now", time spent on specific program pages, and application conversion funnel dropout rates.
33: 
34: ---
```

## Assistant (Build · Kimi K2.6 · 22.6s)

_Thinking:_

Now I need to create the Zustand store. It should handle auth (user with role STUDENT or ADMIN), leads, applications, and emails. Since we're frontend-only, I'll use localStorage persistence where appropriate, but for simplicity and SSR safety in Next.js, I'll start with in-memory state and hydrate from localStorage on mount, or just use in-memory for the demo. Actually, to make the demo robust, I'll use a simple pattern: initialize from localStorage in a useEffect, but default to some mock data for the student dashboard.

Let me create the store, then the UI components.

**Tool: write**

**Input:**

**Input:**
```json
{
  "content": "\"use client\";\n\nimport * as React from \"react\";\n\ntype Theme = \"dark\" | \"light\" | \"system\";\n\ninterface ThemeProviderProps {\n  children: React.ReactNode;\n  defaultTheme?: Theme;\n  enableSystem?: boolean;\n}\n\nexport function ThemeProvider({\n  children,\n  defaultTheme = \"system\",\n}: ThemeProviderProps) {\n  const [theme, setTheme] = React.useState<Theme>(defaultTheme);\n  const [mounted, setMounted] = React.useState(false);\n\n  React.useEffect(() => {\n    const root = document.documentElement;\n    const saved = localStorage.getItem(\"hs-theme\") as Theme | null;\n    const initial = saved || defaultTheme;\n    setTheme(initial);\n    applyTheme(initial);\n    setMounted(true);\n  }, [defaultTheme]);\n\n  const applyTheme = (t: Theme) => {\n    const root = document.documentElement;\n    const systemDark = window.matchMedia(\"(prefers-color-scheme: dark)\").matches;\n    const isDark = t === \"dark\" || (t === \"system\" && systemDark);\n    if (isDark) {\n      root.classList.add(\"dark\");\n    } else {\n      root.classList.remove(\"dark\");\n    }\n  };\n\n  const setAndApply = (t: Theme) => {\n    setTheme(t);\n    localStorage.setItem(\"hs-theme\", t);\n    applyTheme(t);\n  };\n\n  if (!mounted) {\n    return <>{children}</>;\n  }\n\n  return (\n    <ThemeContext.Provider value={{ theme, setTheme: setAndApply }}>\n      {children}\n    </ThemeContext.Provider>\n  );\n}\n\nconst ThemeContext = React.createContext<{\n  theme: Theme;\n  setTheme: (theme: Theme) => void;\n}>({ theme: \"system\", setTheme: () => {} });\n\nexport function useTheme() {\n  return React.useContext(ThemeContext);\n}\n",
  "filePath": "C:\\Users\\carta\\Main\\WORK\\HS_test\\hs-clone\\src\\components\\theme-provider.tsx"
}
```

_Thinking:_

The dynamic import with `.then(m => m.ApplyModalTrigger)` should work but is a bit complex. In Next.js 15+, params is indeed a Promise. The `generateStaticParams` is correct.

However, I just realized that I used `dynamic` import inside the same file after the component definition, and the imports at the top. This might cause issues because the file is a Server Component and then I'm importing client components via dynamic at the bottom. Actually, `dynamic` is fine in server components as long as the imported component is a client component. It should work.

But wait, the file has `import dynamic from "next/dynamic";` at the bottom after the component. In TypeScript/Next.js, imports must be at the top. The file structure is invalid because imports are after code. I need to fix this.

Let me re-read the file and fix it.

```
1: import jwt from "jsonwebtoken";
2: import { NextRequest, NextResponse } from "next/server";
3: 
4: const JWT_SECRET = process.env.JWT_SECRET || "dev-secret-change-in-prod";
5: 
6: export type JWTPayload = {
7:   userId: string;
8:   email: string;
9:   role: string;
10:   iat: number;
11:   exp: number;
12: };
13: 
14: export function signToken(payload: { userId: string; email: string; role: string }): string {
15:   return jwt.sign(payload, JWT_SECRET, { expiresIn: "7d" });
16: }
17: 
18: export function verifyToken(token: string): JWTPayload {
19:   return jwt.verify(token, JWT_SECRET) as JWTPayload;
20: }
21: 
22: export function getAuthUser(req: NextRequest) {
23:   const token = req.cookies.get("hs_token")?.value;
24:   if (!token) return null;
25:   try {
26:     return verifyToken(token);
27:   } catch {
28:     return null;
29:   }
30: }
31: 
32: export function requireAuth(req: NextRequest) {
33:   const user = getAuthUser(req);
34:   if (!user) {
35:     return { error: NextResponse.json({ error: "Unauthorized" }, { status: 401 }), user: null };
36:   }
37:   return { error: null, user };
38: }
39: 
40: export function requireRole(req: NextRequest, role: string) {
41:   const auth = requireAuth(req);
42:   if (auth.error) return auth;
43:   if (auth.user.role !== role) {
44:     return { error: NextResponse.json({ error: "Forbidden" }, { status: 403 }), user: null };
45:   }
46:   return auth;
47: }

(End of file - total 47 lines)
</content>
```

```
1: import { NextResponse } from "next/server";
2: import bcrypt from "bcryptjs";
3: import { prisma } from "@/lib/prisma";
4: import { signToken } from "@/lib/auth";
5: 
6: export async function POST(request: Request) {
7:   try {
8:     const { email, password } = await request.json();
9:     if (!email || !password) {
10:       return NextResponse.json({ error: "Missing fields" }, { status: 400 });
11:     }
12: 
13:     const user = await prisma.user.findUnique({ where: { email } });
14:     if (!user) {
15:       return NextResponse.json({ error: "Invalid credentials" }, { status: 401 });
16:     }
17: 
18:     const valid = await bcrypt.compare(password, user.password);
19:     if (!valid) {
20:       return NextResponse.json({ error: "Invalid credentials" }, { status: 401 });
21:     }
22: 
23:     const token = signToken({ userId: user.id, email: user.email, role: user.role });
24: 
25:     const response = NextResponse.json({
26:       user: { id: user.id, email: user.email, firstName: user.firstName, lastName: user.lastName, role: user.role },
27:     });
28:     response.cookies.set("hs_token", token, {
29:       httpOnly: true,
30:       secure: process.env.NODE_ENV === "production",
31:       sameSite: "lax",
32:       maxAge: 60 * 60 * 24 * 7,
33:       path: "/",
34:     });
35:     return response;
36:   } catch (err) {
37:     console.error("Login error:", err);
38:     return NextResponse.json({ error: "Internal server error" }, { status: 500 });
39:   }
40: }

(End of file - total 40 lines)
```

```
1: import { NextResponse } from "next/server";
2: import bcrypt from "bcryptjs";
3: import { prisma } from "@/lib/prisma";
4: import { signToken } from "@/lib/auth";
5: 
6: export async function POST(request: Request) {
7:   try {
8:     const { email, password, firstName, lastName } = await request.json();
9:     if (!email || !password || !firstName || !lastName) {
10:       return NextResponse.json({ error: "Missing fields" }, { status: 400 });
11:     }
12: 
13:     const existing = await prisma.user.findUnique({ where: { email } });
14:     if (existing) {
15:       return NextResponse.json({ error: "Email already in use" }, { status: 409 });
16:     }
17: 
18:     const hashed = await bcrypt.hash(password, 10);
19:     const user = await prisma.user.create({
20:       data: { email, password: hashed, firstName, lastName },
21:     });
22: 
23:     const token = signToken({ userId: user.id, email: user.email, role: user.role });
24: 
25:     const response = NextResponse.json({ user: { id: user.id, email: user.email, firstName: user.firstName, lastName: user.lastName, role: user.role } });
26:     response.cookies.set("hs_token", token, {
27:       httpOnly: true,
28:       secure: process.env.NODE_ENV === "production",
29:       sameSite: "lax",
30:       maxAge: 60 * 60 * 24 * 7,
31:       path: "/",
32:     });
33:     return response;
34:   } catch (err) {
35:     console.error("Register error:", err);
36:     return NextResponse.json({ error: "Internal server error" }, { status: 500 });
37:   }
```

```
<type>file</type>
<content>
1: "use client";
2: 
3: import * as React from "react";
4: 
5: type Theme = "dark" | "light" | "system";
6: 
7: interface ThemeProviderProps {
8:   children: React.ReactNode;
9:   defaultTheme?: Theme;
10:   enableSystem?: boolean;
11: }
12: 
13: export function ThemeProvider({
14:   children,
15:   defaultTheme = "system",
16: }: ThemeProviderProps) {
17:   const [theme, setTheme] = React.useState<Theme>(defaultTheme);
18:   const [mounted, setMounted] = React.useState(false);
19: 
20:   React.useEffect(() => {
21:     const root = document.documentElement;
22:     const saved = localStorage.getItem("hs-theme") as Theme | null;
23:     const initial = saved || defaultTheme;
24:     setTheme(initial);
25:     applyTheme(initial);
26:     setMounted(true);
27:   }, [defaultTheme]);
28: 
29:   const applyTheme = (t: Theme) => {
30:     const root = document.documentElement;
31:     const systemDark = window.matchMedia("(prefers-color-scheme: dark)").matches;
32:     const isDark = t === "dark" || (t === "system" && systemDark);
33:     if (isDark) {
34:       root.classList.add("dark");
35:     } else {
36:       root.classList.remove("dark");
37:     }
38:   };
39: 
40:   const setAndApply = (t: Theme) => {
41:     setTheme(t);
42:     localStorage.setItem("hs-theme", t);
43:     applyTheme(t);
44:   };
45: 
46:   if (!mounted) {
47:     return <>{children}</>;
48:   }
49: 
50:   return (
51:     <ThemeContext.Provider value={{ theme, setTheme: setAndApply }}>
52:       {children}
53:     </ThemeContext.Provider>
54:   );
55: }
56: 
57: const ThemeContext = React.createContext<{
58:   theme: Theme;
59:   setTheme: (theme: Theme) => void;
60: }>({ theme: "system", setTheme: () => {} });
61: 
62: export function useTheme() {
63:   return React.useContext(ThemeContext);
64: }

(End of file - total 64 lines)
</content>
```

Unless I specify the IDs in the seed.

Actually, looking at the seed file, it uses `upsert` with `where: { slug }` and `update: {}`, `create: p`. If no `id` is provided, Prisma generates a random UUID. So I can't hardcode UUIDs in the frontend.

Alternative approach:
- The apply modal will fetch `/api/programs` to get the actual DB programs with IDs.
- The user selects from the fetched list.
- The static `programs.ts` is used for display/module data only.

\"@/components/ui/tabs\";\nimport { ShieldCheck, Users, ChevronRight } from \"lucide-react\";\n\nconst STAGES = [\n  \"SUBMITTED\",\n  \"INTERVIEW_SCHEDULED\",\n  \"ACCEPTED\",\n  \"ENROLLED\",\n] as const;\n\nconst NEXT_STAGE: Record<string, string | null> = {\n  SUBMITTED: \"INTERVIEW_SCHEDULED\",\n  INTERVIEW_SCHEDULED: \"ACCEPTED\",\n  ACCEPTED: \"ENROLLED\",\n  ENROLLED: null,\n};\n\nconst STAGE_LABELS: Record<string, string> = {\n  SUBMITTED: \"Submitted\",\n  INTERVIEW_SCHEDULED: \"Interview Scheduled\",\n  ACCEPTED: \"Accepted\",\n  ENROLLED: \"Enrolled\",\n};\n\nexport default function AdminPage() {\n  const router = useRouter();\n  const user = useStore((s) => s.user);\n  const [applications, setApplications] = useState<ApiApplication[]>([]);\n  const [leads, setLeads] = useState<ApiLead[]>([]);\n  const [loading, setLoading] = useState(true);\n  const [error, setError] = useState(\"\");\n\n  useEffect(() => {\n    if (!user || user.role !== \"ADMIN\") {\n      router.push(\"/login\");\n      return;\n    }\n    Promise.all([fetchApplications(), fetchLeads()])\n      .then(([apps, ls]) => {\n        setApplications(apps);\n        setLeads(ls);\n      })\n      .catch(() => setError(\"Failed to load admin data\"))\n      .finally(() => setLoading(false));\n  }, [user, router]);\n\n  if (!user || user.role !== \"ADMIN\") return null;\n\n  const advance = async (app: ApiApplication) => {\n    const next = NEXT_STAGE[app.status];\n    if (!next) return;\n    try {\n      const updated = await updateApplication(app.id, { status: next });\n      setApplications((prev) =>\n        prev.map((a) => (a.id === updated.id ? updated : a))\n      );\n    } catch {\n      setError(\"Failed to update status\");\n    }\n  };\n\n  return (\n    <div font-bold tracking-tight\">Admin CRM</h1>\n      </div>\n\n      {error && <p className=\"mb-4 text-sm text-destructive\">{error}</p>}\n\n      <Tabs defaultValue=\"applications\">\n        <TabsList>\n          <TabsTrigger value=\"applications\">Applications</TabsTrigger>\n          <TabsTrigger value=\"leads\">Leads</TabsTrigger>\n        </TabsList>\n\n        <TabsContent gap-3\">\n                <div className=\"flex items-center justify-between\">\n                  <h3 className=\"text-sm font-semibold uppercase tracking-wider text-muted-foreground\">\n                    {STAGE_LABELS[stage]}\n                  </h3>\n                  <Badge variant=\"outline\">\n                    {applications.filter((a) => a.status === stage).length}\n .map((app) => (\n                      <Card key={app.id} className=\"border-l-4 border-l-brand\">\n                        <CardContent className=\"p-4\">\n                          <p className=\"font-medium\">\n                            {app.user.firstName} {app.user.lastName}\n                          </p>\n                          <p className=\"text-xs text-muted-foreground\">\n                            {app.user.email}\n                          </p>\n                          <div className=\"mt-2 flex flex-wrap gap-2 text-xs text-muted-foreground\">\n                            <span>{app.program.title}</span>\n                            <span>•</span>\n                            <span>{app.campus}</span>\n Also, I need to make sure the `admin/page.tsx` doesn't have a hydration issue with `applications.find` inside the render for leads. It should be fine.

Another thing: The `ApplyModal` and `BrochureModal` require the user to be logged in to submit because the backend APIs for `createApplication` and `createLead` may or may not require auth.

Looking at the backend:
- `POST /api/applications` requires auth (`getAuthUser`).
- `POST /api/leads` does NOT require auth. Good.
- `GET /api/programs` does NOT require auth. Good.

So the Apply Modal will fail if the user is not logged in. That's actually correct per the PRD (Apply Now should lead to application, which implies being a user). But for the demo, we might want to show a message or redirect. For now, the error will show "Unauthorized" which is fine.

Wait, the PRD says: "Anonymous Visitor → Discovers Programs → Applies → Admin Reviews in CRM → Student Logs In & Sees Dashboard". The current backend requires auth to apply. This is a backend limitation. Since I'm frontend-only, I can't change the backend. I'll leave it as is. The frontend will show the error from the API.

Actually, the `createLead` (brochure download) works without auth, which is good for the anonymous visitor flow.

Let me now run `npm run build` to check for TypeScript and build errors.

## Assistant (Build · Kimi K2.6 · 11.4s)

_Thinking:_

Build failed because `ssr: false` is not allowed with `next/dynamic` in Server Components in Next.js 16. I need to move the dynamic imports into a client component or remove `ssr: false`. Since the parent is a Server Component, I can just import a wrapper client component that itself renders the triggers.

The easiest fix: Create a single client component `src/components/program-detail-actions.tsx` that imports `ApplyModal` and `BrochureModal` directly and renders both buttons. Then import that wrapper normally (not dynamic) into the server page.

Let me fix this.

## Assistant (Build · Kimi K2.6 · 20.1s)

_Thinking:_

I need to update the Button component to support `asChild`. I'll use the `React.Children.only` pattern with `React.cloneElement`. This is a common pattern.

**Tool: write**

**Input:**
```json
{
  "content": "import * as React from \"react\";\nimport { cn } from \"@/lib/utils\";\n\nexport interface ButtonProps\n  extends React.ButtonHTMLAttributes<HTMLButtonElement> {\n  variant?:\n    | \"default\"\n    | \"destructive\"\n    | \"outline\"\n    | \"secondary\"\n    | \"ghost\"\n    | \"link\"\n    | \"brand\";\n  size?: \"default\" | \"sm\" | \"lg\" | \"icon\";\n  asChild?: boolean;\n}\n\nconst Button = React.forwardRef<HTMLButtonElement, ButtonProps>(\n  ({ className, variant = \"default\", size = \"default\", asChild = false, children, ...props }, ref) => {\n    const variants = {\n      default:\n        \"bg-primary text-primary-foreground hover:bg-primary/90\",\n      destructive:\n        \"bg-destructive text-destructive-foreground hover:bg-destructive/90\",\n      outline:\n        \"border border-input bg-background hover:bg-accent hover:text-accent-foreground\",\n      secondary:\n        \"bg-secondary text-secondary-foreground hover:bg-secondary/80\",\n      ghost:\n        \"hover:bg-accent hover:text-accent-foreground\",\n      link:\n        \"text-primary underline-offset-4 hover:underline\",\n      brand:\n        \"bg-brand text-brand-foreground hover:bg-brand/90\",\n    };\n    const sizes = {\n      default: \"h-10 px-4 py-2\",\n      sm: \"h-9 rounded-md px-3\",\n      lg: \"h-11 rounded-md px-8\",\n      icon: \"h-10 w-10\",\n    };\n    const classes = cn(\n      \"inline-flex items-center justify-center gap-2 whitespace-nowrap rounded-md text-sm font-medium transition-colors focus-visible:outline-none focus-visible:ring-2 focus-visible:ring-ring focus-visible:ring-offset-2 disabled:pointer-events-none disabled:opacity-50\",\n      variants[variant],\n      sizes[size],\n      className\n    );\n\n    if (asChild && React.isValidElement(children)) {\n      return React.cloneElement(children as React.ReactElement<any>, {\n        className: cn(classes, (children as React.ReactElement<any>).props.className),\n        ref,\n        ...props,\n      });\n    }\n\n    return (\n      <button className={classes} ref={ref} {...props}>\n        {children}\n      </button>\n    );\n  }\n);\nButton.displayName = \"Button\";\n\nexport { Button };\n",
  "filePath": "C:\\Users\\carta\\Main\\WORK\\HS_test\\src\\components\\ui\\button.tsx"
}
```

**Foundation**
- Theme provider with dark/light/system toggle

- Documents checklist (English cert, transcripts, visa, health insurance)

**Admin CRM (`/admin`)**

- Leads table from `GET /api/leads`

**Mock Email Service (`/admin/emails`)**
- Viewer for all sent emails fetched from `GET /api/mock-emails`

All frontend files live in the project root (`C:\Users\carta\Main\WORK\HS_test`), and `docs/progress.log` has been updated. The `next build` completes cleanly with static generation for all program pages.
